     <p>The <a href="/wiki/UW%E2%80%93Madison_Geology_Museum" title="UW–Madison Geology Museum">Geology Museum</a> features rocks, minerals, and fossils from around the world. Highlights include a blacklight room, a walk-through cave, and a fragment of the <a href="/wiki/Meteor_Crater" title="Meteor Crater">Barringer meteorite</a>. Some noteworthy fossils include the first dinosaur skeleton assembled in Wisconsin (an <i><a href="/wiki/Edmontosaurus" title="Edmontosaurus">Edmontosaurus</a></i>), a <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">shark</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Squalicorax" title="Squalicorax">Squalicorax</a></i>) and a floating colony of <a href="/wiki/Crinoids" title="Crinoids" class="mw-redirect">sea lilies</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Uintacrinus" title="Uintacrinus">Uintacrinus</a></i>), both from the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> chalk of <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a>, and the Boaz <a href="/wiki/Mastodon" title="Mastodon">Mastodon</a>, a found on a farm in southwestern Wisconsin in 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Chazen_Museum_of_Art" title="Chazen Museum of Art">Chazen Museum of Art</a>, formerly the Elvehjem Museum of Art, maintains a collection of paintings, drawings, sculpture, prints and photographs spanning over 700 years of art.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's Zoological Museum maintains a collection of approximately 500,000 zoological specimens, which can be used for research and instruction. A special collection contains skeletons, artifacts, and research papers associated with the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Gal&aacute;pagos Islands">Gal&aacute;pagos Islands</a>. Since 1978, the UW–Madison Zoological Museum has been one of only three museums granted permission by the Ecuadoran Government to collect anatomical specimens from the Gal&aacute;pagos Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The L. R. Ingersoll Physics Museum contains a range of exhibits demonstrating <a href="/wiki/Classical_physics" title="Classical physics">classical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_physics" title="Modern physics">modern physics</a>. Many of the exhibits allow for hands-on interaction by visitors. The museum also has a number of historical instruments and pictures on display.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effigy_mounds">Effigy mounds</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Effigy mounds">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG/220px-Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG/330px-Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG/440px-Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Willow Drive Effigy Mounds
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UW-Madison claims more distinct archaeological sites than on any other university campus.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus contains four clusters of <a href="/wiki/Effigy_mound" title="Effigy mound">effigy mound</a> located at Observatory Hill, Willow Drive, Picnic Point and Eagle Heights. These sites, reflecting thousands of years of human habitation in the area, have survived to a greater or lesser degree on campus, depending on location and past building activities. Surviving sites are marked and fenced on the campus, ensuring that they are not disturbed. Wisconsin statutes protect effigy mounds by giving them a five-foot buffer zone.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison_Lakeshore_Nature_Preserve" title="University of Wisconsin–Madison Lakeshore Nature Preserve">Lakeshore Nature Preserve Committee</a> is endeavoring to “…safeguard beloved cultural landscapes,” through aggressive enforcement of measures for the preservation of such zones and advocating for broader buffers where possible.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers" title="Wisconsin Badgers">Wisconsin Badgers</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Wisconsin_Waving_W.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/University_of_Wisconsin_Waving_W.svg/170px-University_of_Wisconsin_Waving_W.svg.png" width="170" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/University_of_Wisconsin_Waving_W.svg/255px-University_of_Wisconsin_Waving_W.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/University_of_Wisconsin_Waving_W.svg/340px-University_of_Wisconsin_Waving_W.svg.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Wisconsin_Waving_W.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Wisconsin Badgers &quot;Motion W&quot; logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Wisconsin–Madison sports teams participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Division_I-A" title="Division I-A" class="mw-redirect">Division I-A</a>. With the exception of men's and women's hockey and men and lightweight women's <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_Crew" title="Wisconsin Badgers Crew">Wisconsin Badgers Crew</a>, the university's athletic programs compete in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>. Both <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">hockey</a> programs compete in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Western Collegiate Hockey Association">Western Collegiate Hockey Association</a>, while the <sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> men's and lightweight women's crew programs compete in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Association_of_Rowing_Colleges" title="Eastern Association of Rowing Colleges">Eastern Association of Rowing Colleges</a>. The school's <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a> is <i><a href="/wiki/On,_Wisconsin!" title="On, Wisconsin!">On, Wisconsin!</a></i>. The school's mascot is Buckingham U. Badger, commonly referred to as &quot;<a href="/wiki/Bucky_Badger" title="Bucky Badger">Bucky Badger</a>&quot;. The athletic director is <a href="/wiki/Barry_Alvarez" title="Barry Alvarez">Barry Alvarez</a>.</p> 
     <p>2005–2006 marked the first time in school history that four Badger teams won national championships in the same academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> In the fall, the men's cross country team won its fourth national championship. The winter season was highlighted by the men's and women's ice hockey teams both winning national titles. The year was capped off in the spring with the women's lightweight crew taking its third straight <a href="/wiki/Intercollegiate_Rowing_Association" title="Intercollegiate Rowing Association">Intercollegiate Rowing Association</a> national crown. In 2008, both men's and women's crew teams claimed national titles.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_football" title="Wisconsin Badgers football">Wisconsin Badgers football</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg/220px-Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg/330px-Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg/440px-Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Camp_Randall_Stadium" title="Camp Randall Stadium">Camp Randall Stadium</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Badgers play <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Randall_Stadium" title="Camp Randall Stadium">Camp Randall Stadium</a>. The head coach is <a href="/wiki/Gary_Andersen" title="Gary Andersen">Gary Andersen</a>. Before the fourth quarter of every game at Camp Randall, the crowd jumps around to <a href="/wiki/House_of_Pain" title="House of Pain">House of Pain</a>'s song &quot;<a href="/wiki/Jump_Around" title="Jump Around">Jump Around</a>&quot;. After every game, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin_Marching_Band" title="University of Wisconsin Marching Band">University of Wisconsin Marching Band</a> plays popular songs during the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin_Marching_Band#Traditions" title="University of Wisconsin Marching Band">Fifth Quarter</a>. The Badgers won three <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl</a> Championships under Alvarez in 1994, 1999, and 2000. In 2006, Bielema led the Badgers to a school record 11-win regular season and to 12 overall wins, defeating <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arkansas" title="University of Arkansas">Arkansas</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Capital_One_Bowl" title="Capital One Bowl">Capital One Bowl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> The Badgers lost to <a href="/wiki/Texas_Christian_University" title="Texas Christian University">TCU</a> in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl</a> Championship on January 1, 2011. In the 2011 season, the Badgers defended the B1G championship title to go to the 2012 Rose Bowl Championship. The Badgers lost to Oregon 45–38 in the highest-scoring Rose Bowl of all time.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_basketball">Men's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Men's basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Kohl_Center_inside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kohl_Center_inside.jpg/220px-Kohl_Center_inside.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kohl_Center_inside.jpg/330px-Kohl_Center_inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kohl_Center_inside.jpg/440px-Kohl_Center_inside.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Kohl_Center_inside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Men's basketball game as seen from the student section at the 
        <a href="/wiki/Kohl_Center" title="Kohl Center">Kohl Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_men%27s_basketball" title="Wisconsin Badgers men's basketball">Wisconsin Badgers men's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Badgers have made 13 consecutive appearances at the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournament</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four" class="mw-redirect">Final Four</a> visit in 2000, an <a href="/wiki/Elite_Eight" title="Elite Eight">Elite Eight</a> appearance in 2005, and a Sweet Sixteen appearance in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Badgers' head coach <a href="/wiki/Bo_Ryan" title="Bo Ryan">Bo Ryan</a> has coached the team since 2001. The <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers" title="Wisconsin Badgers">Badgers</a> play at the <a href="/wiki/Kohl_Center" title="Kohl Center">Kohl Center</a>, where the student fans are known as the <a href="/wiki/Grateful_Red" title="Grateful Red">Grateful Red</a>. In the 2006–2007 season, the Badgers attained their highest AP ranking in school history (#1 Feb. 19–25), garnering 35 first-place votes.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The Badgers' earned their only NCAA National Championship in 1941.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women.27s_basketball">Women's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Women's basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_women%27s_basketball" title="Wisconsin Badgers women's basketball">Wisconsin Badgers women's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The women's basketball team plays at the <a href="/wiki/Kohl_Center" title="Kohl Center">Kohl Center</a>. The 2006–2007 season was a record-setting year, with the Badgers recording 23 wins and becoming the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Invitation_Tournament" title="Women's National Invitation Tournament">WNIT</a> runners-up.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ice_hockey">Ice hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ice hockey">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Wisconsin Badgers men's ice hockey">Wisconsin Badgers men's ice hockey</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg/220px-Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg/330px-Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg/440px-Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Men's 
        <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> game played at the 
        <a href="/wiki/Kohl_Center" title="Kohl Center">Kohl Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Badger ice hockey first became a men's varsity sport in 1922. Although dropped after the 1934–35 season, it again became a varsity sport in the 1963–64 season. The men's team played in the <a href="/wiki/Alliant_Energy_Center" title="Alliant Energy Center">Dane County Coliseum</a> until moving to the <a href="/wiki/Kohl_Center" title="Kohl Center">Kohl Center</a> (capacity 15,237) in the fall of 1998. The first ice hockey game played at the Kohl was the Hall of Fame game against the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">University of Notre Dame</a>. The men's team perennially leads the nation in college hockey attendance, and set an NCAA attendance record (averaging 14,430) during the 2006–07 season, surpassing their previous record set the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Bob_Johnson_(ice_hockey_b._1931)" title="Bob Johnson (ice hockey b. 1931)" class="mw-redirect">Bob Johnson</a>, nicknamed &quot;Badger Bob&quot; by fans, took over the reins in 1966. Johnson coached the Badger men to three national championships in 1973, 1977 and 1981. Jeff Sauer coached the Badger men to two more titles in 1983 and 1990. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Eaves" title="Mike Eaves">Mike Eaves</a>, member of the 1977 NCAA title team, coached the Badger men's team to its sixth national championship in 2006. The six Badger titles rank 4th in NCAA men's ice hockey history.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Eaves' 2010 squad advanced to the national championship game during the Badgers' 11th appearance in the men's <a href="/wiki/Frozen_Four" title="Frozen Four" class="mw-redirect">Frozen Four</a> before bowing to <a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>.</p> 
     <p>The school's strong ice hockey tradition gained another dimension with the addition of a women's team that began play in the 1999–2000 season. Coached by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Johnson_(hockey_player)" title="Mark Johnson (hockey player)" class="mw-redirect">Mark Johnson</a>, son of &quot;Badger Bob&quot; and another member of the men's 1977 title team, the Badger women won their first NCAA championship on March 26, 2006. The dual 2006 titles marked the first time that both the men's and women's Division I NCAA hockey titles were won by the same school in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The women's team repeated as national champions in 2007 with a victory over the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota-Duluth" title="University of Minnesota-Duluth" class="mw-redirect">University of Minnesota-Duluth</a> on March 18 at <a href="/wiki/Herb_Brooks_Arena" title="Herb Brooks Arena">Herb Brooks Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Placid,_NY" title="Lake Placid, NY" class="mw-redirect">Lake Placid, NY</a>. With a 5–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Mercyhurst" title="Mercyhurst" class="mw-redirect">Mercyhurst</a> in the 2009 Women's Frozen Four final in Boston, the Badger women added their third NCAA title.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers" title="Wisconsin Badgers">Wisconsin Badgers</a> most notable rivalry within the Big Ten is with the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers">University of Minnesota</a>, which is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_NCAA_college_football_rivalry_games" title="List of NCAA college football rivalry games">most-played rivalry</a> in Division 1-A football.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> In their annual <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> game, the teams compete for <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe" title="Paul Bunyan's Axe">Paul Bunyan's Axe</a>. The two universities also compete in the <i>Border Battle</i>, a year-long athletic competition in which each team's wins earn points for their university.</p> 
     <p>Men's basketball rivalries include <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_basketball" title="Michigan State Spartans men's basketball">Michigan State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Fighting_Illini_men%27s_basketball" title="Illinois Fighting Illini men's basketball">Illinois</a> and non-conference, in-state <a href="/wiki/Marquette_Golden_Eagles_men%27s_basketball" title="Marquette Golden Eagles men's basketball">Marquette</a>.</p> 
     <p>The long-standing football rivalry between the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Iowa" title="University of Iowa">University of Iowa</a> and Wisconsin–Madison was finally recognized in 2004, with the winner of their game being awarded the <a href="/wiki/Heartland_Trophy" title="Heartland Trophy" class="mw-redirect">Heartland Trophy</a>.</p> 
     <p>The Wisconsin–Madison men's and women's hockey teams' most recognized rivals are the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gophers" title="Golden Gophers" class="mw-redirect">Golden Gophers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota" title="University of Minnesota">University of Minnesota</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fighting_Sioux" title="Fighting Sioux" class="mw-redirect">Fighting Sioux</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Dakota" title="University of North Dakota">University of North Dakota</a>. Other rivals include the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">University of Denver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_College" title="Colorado College">Colorado College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Tech_University" title="Michigan Tech University" class="mw-redirect">Michigan Tech</a>, University of Minnesota Duluth, and <a href="/wiki/St._Cloud_State_University" title="St. Cloud State University">St. Cloud State</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The school mascot is an <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">anthropomorphized</a> <a href="/wiki/Badger" title="Badger">badger</a> named <a href="/wiki/Bucky_Badger" title="Bucky Badger">Bucky</a> who dons a sweater affixed with the UW–Madison athletic logo (currently the red &quot;Motion W&quot;). Beginning in 1890, the university's first Bucky Badger was a live, temperamental and unruly <a href="/wiki/Badger" title="Badger">badger</a> who was quickly retired. Although the nickname of the Wisconsin teams remained the &quot;Badgers&quot;, it was not until Art Evans drew the early caricature version of Bucky in 1940 that today's recognizable image of Bucky was adopted. In 1949, a contest was held to name the mascot, but no consensus was reached after only a few entries were received. In reaction, the contest committee chose the name Buckingham U. Badger, or &quot;Bucky,&quot; for short.</p> 
     <p>At Wisconsin football games in the 1920s live mascots were used to inspire fans. The animals used included a black bear, a bonnet monkey, and live badgers. 1949 was the first year a student sporting a papier-m&acirc;ch&eacute; badger head appeared; this subsequently replaced the use of live badgers.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The team's nickname originates from the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_nicknames" title="List of U.S. state nicknames">state nickname</a>. In the 1820s, many lead miners and their families lived in the mines in which they worked until adequate above-ground shelters were built, and thus were compared to badgers.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2009, John Fromstein produced &quot;Being Bucky&quot; a documentary that followed the seven Wisconsin students who take on the role of Bucky Badger. The documentary was meant to show the life and background of being a mascot at a major university. &quot;Being Bucky&quot; won &quot;Best Documentary Film&quot; at the Wisconsin Film Fest and went on to play in local Wisconsin movie theaters.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Over 750 student organizations or clubs register with the Center for Leadership and Involvement (CFLI) at UW–Madison each year.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>All-Campus Party (ACP)</b> Every spring, the Wisconsin Alumni Association (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.uwalumni.com/">WAA</a>) and the Wisconsin Alumni Student Board (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.uwalumni.com/wasb">WASB</a>) put on a free, alcohol alternative, week-long series of events for the entire student body. They partner with local businesses, student organizations, and national corporations to sponsor All-Campus Party (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.allcampusparty.com/index.html">ACP</a>). This is a celebration of University of Wisconsin–Madison for students, created by students. The week includes featured events specifically designed and put together by members of WASB, in addition to many other events put on by the varying sponsors and student organizations. The featured events include:</p> 
     <p><i>Breakfast with Bucky</i>- A free, continental, sponsored breakfast for all students. There are multiple locations on campus where breakfast is served to accommodate as many students as possible.</p> 
     <p><i>All-Campus Idol</i>- With a format similar to the popular television show, <a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a>, this singing talent competition searches for the best act on campus. Auditions are held looking for the top ten contestants to perform and compete on stage in front of a live audience. At the end of the show, the audience can text in their votes to determine the winner.</p> 
     <p><i>Wear Red Get Fed/ Bucky State Fair</i>- Students are encouraged to wear red this day and receive free pizza in Library Mall. Rock wall climbing, Gladiator fighting, and other fun activities are there as well. Student organizations are encouraged to sign-up and host a booth in Library Mall and promote their organization as well.</p> 
     <p><i>Club Bucky</i> – A live DJ, free food, and lots of dancing! A club atmosphere is provided for students as they dance the night away.</p> 
     <p><i>Buckystock</i> – Previously known as &quot;Bucky's Blowout Concert&quot; A free, concert in Library Mall for all. The artist changes each year; previous performers include Violent Femmes (2005), Common (2006), Ben Kweller (2007), Talib Kweli (2008), Ok Go (2009), We the Living, and the Grace Weber Band (2010).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_publications">Student publications</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Student publications">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>UW–Madison is the only American university to have two competing daily <a href="/wiki/Student_newspapers" title="Student newspapers" class="mw-redirect">student newspapers</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Cardinal" title="The Daily Cardinal">The Daily Cardinal</a></i>, founded in 1892 and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Badger_Herald" title="The Badger Herald">The Badger Herald</a></i>, founded in 1969. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Onion" title="The Onion">The Onion</a></i> was founded in 1988 by two UW–Madison juniors, and was published in Madison before moving to New York City in 2001. It is also the home of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Madison_Misnomer" title="The Madison Misnomer">The Madison Misnomer</a></i>, an undergraduate comedy newspaper, founded in 2007.</p> 
     <p>UW-Madison is also home to one of only two nationally distributed undergraduate international studies journals in the country. The Journal of Undergraduate International Studies (JUIS) is a competitive publication that features peer-reviewed academic articles. It was founded in 2003 by David Coddon with the support of the University of Wisconsin–Madison Leadership Trust.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_radio">Campus radio</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Campus radio">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The University of Wisconsin–Madison campus radio station is <a href="/wiki/WSUM" title="WSUM">WSUM</a> 91.7 FM, &quot;The Snake on the Lake&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> Historically, UW–Madison has been home to a collection of student run radio stations, a number of which stopped broadcasting after run-ins with the United States <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a> (FCC). The current radio station, WSUM, began in 1997 in a <a href="/wiki/Webcast" title="Webcast">webcast</a> only format because of the prolonged battle to get an FCC license and construct a tower. This lasted five years until February 22, 2002, when the station started broadcasting over <a href="/wiki/Frequency_modulation" title="Frequency modulation">FM</a> airwaves at 91.7 from its tower in <a href="/wiki/Montrose,_Wisconsin" title="Montrose, Wisconsin">Montrose, Wisconsin</a>. The radio station currently has around 150 volunteer DJs and 8 paid managers. All UW–Madison students, as well as a limited number of community members, are eligible to participate in running the station. WSUM remains entirely free format, which means that the on-air personnel can showcase a large variety of music and talk programming at their discretion with few limitations. WSUM has garnered many awards from the Wisconsin Broadcasters Association for their news, play-by-play broadcasts of Badger athletic events, and unique <a href="/wiki/Public_service_announcements" title="Public service announcements" class="mw-redirect">public service announcements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Party_school.22_image">&quot;Party school&quot; image</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: &quot;Party school&quot; image">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2010 Wisconsin was named the number three &quot;<a href="/wiki/Party_school" title="Party school">party school</a>&quot; by <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i> magazine,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> and number 12 by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> UW–Madison has long held a reputation for academics, political activism, and drinking; the last of these can be understood in the context of the state's traditionally high level of alcohol consumption in general.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The festive mentality is most notably displayed with the annual <a href="/wiki/Mifflin_Street_Block_Party" title="Mifflin Street Block Party">Mifflin Street Block Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/State_Street_Halloween_Party" title="State Street Halloween Party">State Street Halloween Party</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Mifflin_Street_Block_Party" title="Mifflin Street Block Party">Mifflin Street Block Party</a>, which began in the 1960s as a counterculture event, is today a spring semester finals week kickoff. Both events are commonly attended by tens of thousands of partiers, including many who come from out of state. Following a non-political riot that developed at the 1996 Mifflin Street Block Party, it was forcibly canceled by the city, but was later reinstated. At the 2011 party, two people were stabbed, leading the city to consider banning the party. The city decided to allow it to continue in the future, under a zero-tolerance policy.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="MTV.27s_College_Life">MTV's <i>College Life</i></span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: MTV's College Life">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>On April 13, 2009, MTV premiered the <a href="/wiki/Reality_series" title="Reality series" class="mw-redirect">reality series</a> <i><a href="/wiki/College_Life" title="College Life">College Life</a></i> about the day-to-day lives of eight UW–Madison freshmen.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> The show was created by UW–Madison alumnus <a href="/wiki/David_Wexler_(writer/director)" title="David Wexler (writer/director)" class="mw-redirect">David Wexler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> According to MTV,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> the students did the filming for the series, but not the editing. During production, the university pulled its support of the show. Subsequently, a disclaimer was aired at the beginning of each episode stating that UW–Madison does not endorse the program. Eight episodes aired as of February 22, 2010.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_people">Notable alumni and people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison_people" title="List of University of Wisconsin–Madison people">List of University of Wisconsin–Madison people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In 2008, UW–Madison had 387,912 living alumni. Although a large number of alumni live in Wisconsin, a significant number live in Illinois, Minnesota, New York, California, and Washington, D.C. UW–Madison also had 15,479 alumni living outside of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-alumni_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alumni-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UW–Madison alumni, faculty, or former faculty have been awarded 19 Nobel Prizes and 34 Pulitzer Prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-alumni_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alumni-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
